Blocking rules take priority\n    39→        over warning rules. {"parentUuid":"b91bddd8-991f-44e0-9b8c-874617d2ec1a","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"4cff8217-4055-4c23-8140-7e344f8eaa3c","agentId":"afe9d1f61c02b1e8d","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01HsDj5a2fqyYUVdyFu65CV4","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Hookify Plugin\n     2→\n     3→Easily create custom hooks to prevent unwanted behaviors by analyzing conversation patterns or from explicit instructions.\n     4→\n     5→## Overview\n     6→\n     7→The hookify plugin makes it simple to create hooks without editing complex `hooks.json` files. Instead, you create lightweight markdown configuration files that define patterns to watch for and messages to show when those patterns match.\n     8→\n     9→**Key features:**\n    10→- 🎯 Analyze conversations to find unwanted behaviors automatically\n    11→- 📝 Simple markdown configuration files with YAML frontmatter\n    12→- 🔍 Regex pattern matching for powerful rules\n    13→- 🚀 No coding required - just describe the behavior\n    14→- 🔄 Easy enable/disable without restarting\n    15→\n    16→## Quick Start\n    17→\n    18→### 1. Create Your First Rule\n    19→\n    20→```bash\n    21→/hookify Warn me when I use rm -rf commands\n    22→```\n    23→\n    24→This analyzes your request and creates `.claude/hookify.warn-rm.local.md`.\n    25→\n    26→### 2. Test It Immediately\n    27→\n    28→**No restart needed!** Rules take effect on the very next tool use.\n    29→\n    30→Ask Claude to run a command that should trigger the rule:\n    31→```\n    32→Run rm -rf /tmp/test\n    33→```\n    34→\n    35→You should see the warning message immediately!\n    36→\n    37→## Usage\n    38→\n    39→### Main Command: /hookify\n    40→\n    41→**With arguments:**\n    42→```\n    43→/hookify Don't use console.log in TypeScript files\n    44→```\n    45→Creates a rule from your explicit instructions.\n    46→\n    47→**Without arguments:**\n    48→```\n    49→/hookify\n    50→```\n    51→Analyzes recent conversation to find behaviors you've corrected or been frustrated by.\n    52→\n    53→### Helper Commands\n    54→\n    55→**List all rules:**\n    56→```\n    57→/hookify:list\n    58→```\n    59→\n    60→**Configure rules interactively:**\n    61→```\n    62→/hookify:configure\n    63→```\n    64→Enable/disable existing rules through an interactive interface.\n    65→\n    66→**Get help:**\n    67→```\n    68→/hookify:help\n    69→```\n    70→\n    71→## Rule Configuration Format\n    72→\n    73→### Simple Rule (Single Pattern)\n    74→\n    75→`.claude/hookify.dangerous-rm.local.md`:\n    76→```markdown\n    77→---\n    78→name: block-dangerous-rm\n    79→enabled: true\n    80→event: bash\n    81→pattern: rm\\s+-rf\n    82→action: block\n    83→---\n    84→\n    85→⚠️ **Dangerous rm command detected!**\n    86→\n    87→This command could delete important files. Please:\n    88→- Verify the path is correct\n    89→- Consider using a safer approach\n    90→- Make sure you have backups\n    91→```\n    92→\n    93→**Action field:**\n    94→- `warn`: Shows warning but allows operation (default)\n    95→- `block`: Prevents operation from executing (PreToolUse) or stops session (Stop events)\n    96→\n    97→### Advanced Rule (Multiple Conditions)\n    98→\n    99→`.claude/hookify.sensitive-files.local.md`:\n   100→```markdown\n   101→---\n   102→name: warn-sensitive-files\n   103→enabled: true\n   104→event: file\n   105→action: warn\n   106→conditions:\n   107→  - field: file_path\n   108→    operator: regex_match\n   109→    pattern: \\.env$|credentials|secrets\n   110→  - field: new_text\n   111→    operator: contains\n   112→    pattern: KEY\n   113→---\n   114→\n   115→🔐 **Sensitive file edit detected!**\n   116→\n   117→Ensure credentials are not hardcoded and file is in .gitignore.\n   118→```\n   119→\n   120→**All conditions must match** for the rule to trigger.\n   121→\n   122→## Event Types\n   123→\n   124→- **`bash`**: Triggers on Bash tool commands\n   125→- **`file`**: Triggers on Edit, Write, MultiEdit tools\n   126→- **`stop`**: Triggers when Claude wants to stop (for completion checks)\n   127→- **`prompt`**: Triggers on user prompt submission\n   128→- **`all`**: Triggers on all events\n   129→\n   130→## Pattern Syntax\n   131→\n   132→Use Python regex syntax:\n   133→\n   134→| Pattern | Matches | Example |\n   135→|---------|---------|---------|\n   136→| `rm\\s+-rf` | rm -rf | rm -rf /tmp |\n   137→| `console\\.log\\(` | console.log( | console.log(\"test\") |\n   138→| `(eval\\|exec)\\(` | eval( or exec( | eval(\"code\") |\n   139→| `\\.env$` | files ending in .env | .env, .env.local |\n   140→| `chmod\\s+777` | chmod 777 | chmod 777 file.txt |\n   141→\n   142→**Tips:**\n   143→- Use `\\s` for whitespace\n   144→- Escape special chars: `\\.` for literal dot\n   145→- Use `|` for OR: `(foo|bar)`\n   146→- Use `.*` to match anything\n   147→- Set `action: block` for dangerous operations\n   148→- Set `action: warn` (or omit) for informational warnings\n   149→\n   150→## Examples\n   151→\n   152→### Example 1: Block Dangerous Commands\n   153→\n   154→```markdown\n   155→---\n   156→name: block-destructive-ops\n   157→enabled: true\n   158→event: bash\n   159→pattern: rm\\s+-rf|dd\\s+if=|mkfs|format\n   160→action: block\n   161→---\n   162→\n   163→🛑 **Destructive operation detected!**\n   164→\n   165→This command can cause data loss. Operation blocked for safety.\n   166→Please verify the exact path and use a safer approach.\n   167→```\n   168→\n   169→**This rule blocks the operation** - Claude will not be allowed to execute these commands.\n   170→\n   171→### Example 2: Warn About Debug Code\n   172→\n   173→```markdown\n   174→---\n   175→name: warn-debug-code\n   176→enabled: true\n   177→event: file\n   178→pattern: console\\.log\\(|debugger;|print\\(\n   179→action: warn\n   180→---\n   181→\n   182→🐛 **Debug code detected**\n   183→\n   184→Remember to remove debugging statements before committing.\n   185→```\n   186→\n   187→**This rule warns but allows** - Claude sees the message but can still proceed.\n   188→\n   189→### Example 3: Require Tests Before Stopping\n   190→\n   191→```markdown\n   192→---\n   193→name: require-tests-run\n   194→enabled: false\n   195→event: stop\n   196→action: block\n   197→conditions:\n   198→  - field: transcript\n   199→    operator: not_contains\n   200→    pattern: npm test|pytest|cargo test\n   201→---\n   202→\n   203→**Tests not detected in transcript!**\n   204→\n   205→Before stopping, please run tests to verify your changes work correctly.\n   206→```\n   207→\n   208→**This blocks Claude from stopping** if no test commands appear in the session transcript. Enable only when you want strict enforcement.\n   209→\n   210→## Advanced Usage\n   211→\n   212→### Multiple Conditions\n   213→\n   214→Check multiple fields simultaneously:\n   215→\n   216→```markdown\n   217→---\n   218→name: api-key-in-typescript\n   219→enabled: true\n   220→event: file\n   221→conditions:\n   222→  - field: file_path\n   223→    operator: regex_match\n   224→    pattern: \\.tsx?$\n   225→  - field: new_text\n   226→    operator: regex_match\n   227→    pattern: (API_KEY|SECRET|TOKEN)\\s*=\\s*[\"']\n   228→---\n   229→\n   230→🔐 **Hardcoded credential in TypeScript!**\n   231→\n   232→Use environment variables instead of hardcoded values.\n   233→```\n   234→\n   235→### Operators Reference\n   236→\n   237→- `regex_match`: Pattern must match (most common)\n   238→- `contains`: String must contain pattern\n   239→- `equals`: Exact string match\n   240→- `not_contains`: String must NOT contain pattern\n   241→- `starts_with`: String starts with pattern\n   242→- `ends_with`: String ends with pattern\n   243→\n   244→### Field Reference\n   245→\n   246→**For bash events:**\n   247→- `command`: The bash command string\n   248→\n   249→**For file events:**\n   250→- `file_path`: Path to file being edited\n   251→- `new_text`: New content being added (Edit, Write)\n   252→- `old_text`: Old content being replaced (Edit only)\n   253→- `content`: File content (Write only)\n   254→\n   255→**For prompt events:**\n   256→- `user_prompt`: The user's submitted prompt text\n   257→\n   258→**For stop events:**\n   259→- Use general matching on session state\n   260→\n   261→## Management\n   262→\n   263→### Enable/Disable Rules\n   264→\n   265→**Temporarily disable:**\n   266→Edit the `.local.md` file and set `enabled: false`\n   267→\n   268→**Re-enable:**\n   269→Set `enabled: true`\n   270→\n   271→**Or use interactive tool:**\n   272→```\n   273→/hookify:configure\n   274→```\n   275→\n   276→### Delete Rules\n   277→\n   278→Simply delete the `.local.md` file:\n   279→```bash\n   280→rm .claude/hookify.my-rule.local.md\n   281→```\n   282→\n   283→### View All Rules\n   284→\n   285→```\n   286→/hookify:list\n   287→```\n   288→\n   289→## Installation\n   290→\n   291→This plugin is part of the Claude Code Marketplace. It should be auto-discovered when the marketplace is installed.\n   292→\n   293→**Manual testing:**\n   294→```bash\n   295→cc --plugin-dir /path/to/hookify\n   296→```\n   297→\n   298→## Requirements\n   299→\n   300→- Python 3.7+\n   301→- No external dependencies (uses stdlib only)\n   302→\n   303→## Troubleshooting\n   304→\n   305→**Rule not triggering:**\n   306→1. Check rule file exists in `.claude/` directory (in project root, not plugin directory)\n   307→2. Verify `enabled: true` in frontmatter\n   308→3. Test regex pattern separately\n   309→4. Rules should work immediately - no restart needed\n   310→5. Try `/hookify:list` to see if rule is loaded\n   311→\n   312→**Import errors:**\n   313→- Ensure Python 3 is available: `python3 --version`\n   314→- Check hookify plugin is installed\n   315→\n   316→**Pattern not matching:**\n   317→- Test regex: `python3 -c \"import re; print(re.search(r'pattern', 'text'))\"`\n   318→- Use unquoted patterns in YAML to avoid escaping issues\n   319→- Start simple, then add complexity\n   320→\n   321→**Hook seems slow:**\n   322→- Keep patterns simple (avoid complex regex)\n   323→- Use specific event types (bash, file) instead of \"all\"\n   324→- Limit number of active rules\n   325→\n   326→## Contributing\n   327→\n   328→Found a useful rule pattern? Consider sharing example files via PR!\n   329→\n   330→## Future Enhancements\n   331→\n   332→- Severity levels (error/warning/info distinctions)\n   333→- Rule templates library\n   334→- Interactive pattern builder\n   335→- Hook testing utilities\n   336→- JSON format support (in addition to markdown)\n   337→\n   338→## License\n   339→\n   340→MIT License\n   341→"}]},"uuid":"7a554a88-b88a-4b39-a09e-96143e970932","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:18:21.337Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"b91bddd8-991f-44e0-9b8c-874617d2ec1a","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

{"parentUuid":"2b6b2cf7-e494-4db2-b3c1-a736d3716632","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"4cff8217-4055-4c23-8140-7e344f8eaa3c","agentId":"afe9d1f61c02b1e8d","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01CKpt3hT5gEH4j7BvMJmTaS","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→name: hook-development\n     3→description: This skill should be used when the user asks to \"create a hook\", \"add a PreToolUse/PostToolUse/Stop hook\", \"validate tool use\", \"implement prompt-based hooks\", \"use ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}\", \"set up event-driven automation\", \"block dangerous commands\", or mentions hook events (PreToolUse, PostToolUse, Stop, SubagentStop, SessionStart, SessionEnd, UserPromptSubmit, PreCompact, Notification). Provides comprehensive guidance for creating and implementing Claude Code plugin hooks with focus on advanced prompt-based hooks API.\n     4→version: 0.1.0\n     5→---\n     6→\n     7→# Hook Development for Claude Code Plugins\n     8→\n     9→## Overview\n    10→\n    11→Hooks are event-driven automation scripts that execute in response to Claude Code events. Use hooks to validate operations, enforce policies, add context, and integrate external tools into workflows.\n    12→\n    13→**Key capabilities:**\n    14→- Validate tool calls before execution (PreToolUse)\n    15→- React to tool results (PostToolUse)\n    16→- Enforce completion standards (Stop, SubagentStop)\n    17→- Load project context (SessionStart)\n    18→- Automate workflows across the development lifecycle\n    19→\n    20→## Hook Types\n    21→\n    22→### Prompt-Based Hooks (Recommended)\n    23→\n    24→Use LLM-driven decision making for context-aware validation:\n    25→\n    26→```json\n    27→{\n    28→  \"type\": \"prompt\",\n    29→  \"prompt\": \"Evaluate if this tool use is appropriate: $TOOL_INPUT\",\n    30→  \"timeout\": 30\n    31→}\n    32→```\n    33→\n    34→**Supported events:** Stop, SubagentStop, UserPromptSubmit, PreToolUse\n    35→\n    36→**Benefits:**\n    37→- Context-aware decisions based on natural language reasoning\n    38→- Flexible evaluation logic without bash scripting\n    39→- Better edge case handling\n    40→- Easier to maintain and extend\n    41→\n    42→### Command Hooks\n    43→\n    44→Execute bash commands for deterministic checks:\n    45→\n    46→```json\n    47→{\n    48→  \"type\": \"command\",\n    49→  \"command\": \"bash ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/scripts/validate.sh\",\n    50→  \"timeout\": 60\n    51→}\n    52→```\n    53→\n    54→**Use for:**\n    55→- Fast deterministic validations\n    56→- File system operations\n    57→- External tool integrations\n    58→- Performance-critical checks\n    59→\n    60→## Hook Configuration Formats\n    61→\n    62→### Plugin hooks.json Format\n    63→\n    64→**For plugin hooks** in `hooks/hooks.json`, use wrapper format:\n    65→\n    66→```json\n    67→{\n    68→  \"description\": \"Brief explanation of hooks (optional)\",\n    69→  \"hooks\": {\n    70→    \"PreToolUse\": [...],\n    71→    \"Stop\": [...],\n    72→    \"SessionStart\": [...]\n    73→  }\n    74→}\n    75→```\n    76→\n    77→**Key points:**\n    78→- `description` field is optional\n    79→- `hooks` field is required wrapper containing actual hook events\n    80→- This is the **plugin-specific format**\n    81→\n    82→**Example:**\n    83→```json\n    84→{\n    85→  \"description\": \"Validation hooks for code quality\",\n    86→  \"hooks\": {\n    87→    \"PreToolUse\": [\n    88→      {\n    89→        \"matcher\": \"Write\",\n    90→        \"hooks\": [\n    91→          {\n    92→            \"type\": \"command\",\n    93→            \"command\": \"${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/hooks/validate.sh\"\n    94→          }\n    95→        ]\n    96→      }\n    97→    ]\n    98→  }\n    99→}\n   100→```\n   101→\n   102→### Settings Format (Direct)\n   103→\n   104→**For user settings** in `.claude/settings.json`, use direct format:\n   105→\n   106→```json\n   107→{\n   108→  \"PreToolUse\": [...],\n   109→  \"Stop\": [...],\n   110→  \"SessionStart\": [...]\n   111→}\n   112→```\n   113→\n   114→**Key points:**\n   115→- No wrapper - events directly at top level\n   116→- No description field\n   117→- This is the **settings format**\n   118→\n   119→**Important:** The examples below show the hook event structure that goes inside either format. For plugin hooks.json, wrap these in `{\"hooks\": {...}}`.\n   120→\n   121→## Hook Events\n   122→\n   123→### PreToolUse\n   124→\n   125→Execute before any tool runs. Use to approve, deny, or modify tool calls.\n   126→\n   127→**Example (prompt-based):**\n   128→```json\n   129→{\n   130→  \"PreToolUse\": [\n   131→    {\n   132→      \"matcher\": \"Write|Edit\",\n   133→      \"hooks\": [\n   134→        {\n   135→          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n   136→          \"prompt\": \"Validate file write safety. Check: system paths, credentials, path traversal, sensitive content. Return 'approve' or 'deny'.\"\n   137→        }\n   138→      ]\n   139→    }\n   140→  ]\n   141→}\n   142→```\n   143→\n   144→**Output for PreToolUse:**\n   145→```json\n   146→{\n   147→  \"hookSpecificOutput\": {\n   148→    \"permissionDecision\": \"allow|deny|ask\",\n   149→    \"updatedInput\": {\"field\": \"modified_value\"}\n   150→  },\n   151→  \"systemMessage\": \"Explanation for Claude\"\n   152→}\n   153→```\n   154→\n   155→### PostToolUse\n   156→\n   157→Execute after tool completes. Use to react to results, provide feedback, or log.\n   158→\n   159→**Example:**\n   160→```json\n   161→{\n   162→  \"PostToolUse\": [\n   163→    {\n   164→      \"matcher\": \"Edit\",\n   165→      \"hooks\": [\n   166→        {\n   167→          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n   168→          \"prompt\": \"Analyze edit result for potential issues: syntax errors, security vulnerabilities, breaking changes. Provide feedback.\"\n   169→        }\n   170→      ]\n   171→    }\n   172→  ]\n   173→}\n   174→```\n   175→\n   176→**Output behavior:**\n   177→- Exit 0: stdout shown in transcript\n   178→- Exit 2: stderr fed back to Claude\n   179→- systemMessage included in context\n   180→\n   181→### Stop\n   182→\n   183→Execute when main agent considers stopping. Use to validate completeness.\n   184→\n   185→**Example:**\n   186→```json\n   187→{\n   188→  \"Stop\": [\n   189→    {\n   190→      \"matcher\": \"*\",\n   191→      \"hooks\": [\n   192→        {\n   193→          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n   194→          \"prompt\": \"Verify task completion: tests run, build succeeded, questions answered. Return 'approve' to stop or 'block' with reason to continue.\"\n   195→        }\n   196→      ]\n   197→    }\n   198→  ]\n   199→}\n   200→```\n   201→\n   202→**Decision output:**\n   203→```json\n   204→{\n   205→  \"decision\": \"approve|block\",\n   206→  \"reason\": \"Explanation\",\n   207→  \"systemMessage\": \"Additional context\"\n   208→}\n   209→```\n   210→\n   211→### SubagentStop\n   212→\n   213→Execute when subagent considers stopping. Use to ensure subagent completed its task.\n   214→\n   215→Similar to Stop hook, but for subagents.\n   216→\n   217→### UserPromptSubmit\n   218→\n   219→Execute when user submits a prompt. Use to add context, validate, or block prompts.\n   220→\n   221→**Example:**\n   222→```json\n   223→{\n   224→  \"UserPromptSubmit\": [\n   225→    {\n   226→      \"matcher\": \"*\",\n   227→      \"hooks\": [\n   228→        {\n   229→          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n   230→          \"prompt\": \"Check if prompt requires security guidance. If discussing auth, permissions, or API security, return relevant warnings.\"\n   231→        }\n   232→      ]\n   233→    }\n   234→  ]\n   235→}\n   236→```\n   237→\n   238→### SessionStart\n   239→\n   240→Execute when Claude Code session begins. Use to load context and set environment.\n   241→\n   242→**Example:**\n   243→```json\n   244→{\n   245→  \"SessionStart\": [\n   246→    {\n   247→      \"matcher\": \"*\",\n   248→      \"hooks\": [\n   249→        {\n   250→          \"type\": \"command\",\n   251→          \"command\": \"bash ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/scripts/load-context.sh\"\n   252→        }\n   253→      ]\n   254→    }\n   255→  ]\n   256→}\n   257→```\n   258→\n   259→**Special capability:** Persist environment variables using `$CLAUDE_ENV_FILE`:\n   260→```bash\n   261→echo \"export PROJECT_TYPE=nodejs\" >> \"$CLAUDE_ENV_FILE\"\n   262→```\n   263→\n   264→See `examples/load-context.sh` for complete example.\n   265→\n   266→### SessionEnd\n   267→\n   268→Execute when session ends. Use for cleanup, logging, and state preservation.\n   269→\n   270→### PreCompact\n   271→\n   272→Execute before context compaction. Use to add critical information to preserve.\n   273→\n   274→### Notification\n   275→\n   276→Execute when Claude sends notifications. Use to react to user notifications.\n   277→\n   278→## Hook Output Format\n   279→\n   280→### Standard Output (All Hooks)\n   281→\n   282→```json\n   283→{\n   284→  \"continue\": true,\n   285→  \"suppressOutput\": false,\n   286→  \"systemMessage\": \"Message for Claude\"\n   287→}\n   288→```\n   289→\n   290→- `continue`: If false, halt processing (default true)\n   291→- `suppressOutput`: Hide output from transcript (default false)\n   292→- `systemMessage`: Message shown to Claude\n   293→\n   294→### Exit Codes\n   295→\n   296→- `0` - Success (stdout shown in transcript)\n   297→- `2` - Blocking error (stderr fed back to Claude)\n   298→- Other - Non-blocking error\n   299→\n   300→## Hook Input Format\n   301→\n   302→All hooks receive JSON via stdin with common fields:\n   303→\n   304→```json\n   305→{\n   306→  \"session_id\": \"abc123\",\n   307→  \"transcript_path\": \"/path/to/transcript.txt\",\n   308→  \"cwd\": \"/current/working/dir\",\n   309→  \"permission_mode\": \"ask|allow\",\n   310→  \"hook_event_name\": \"PreToolUse\"\n   311→}\n   312→```\n   313→\n   314→**Event-specific fields:**\n   315→\n   316→- **PreToolUse/PostToolUse:** `tool_name`, `tool_input`, `tool_result`\n   317→- **UserPromptSubmit:** `user_prompt`\n   318→- **Stop/SubagentStop:** `reason`\n   319→\n   320→Access fields in prompts using `$TOOL_INPUT`, `$TOOL_RESULT`, `$USER_PROMPT`, etc.\n   321→\n   322→## Environment Variables\n   323→\n   324→Available in all command hooks:\n   325→\n   326→- `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` - Project root path\n   327→- `$CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT` - Plugin directory (use for portable paths)\n   328→- `$CLAUDE_ENV_FILE` - SessionStart only: persist env vars here\n   329→- `$CLAUDE_CODE_REMOTE` - Set if running in remote context\n   330→\n   331→**Always use ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT} in hook commands for portability:**\n   332→\n   333→```json\n   334→{\n   335→  \"type\": \"command\",\n   336→  \"command\": \"bash ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/scripts/validate.sh\"\n   337→}\n   338→```\n   339→\n   340→## Plugin Hook Configuration\n   341→\n   342→In plugins, define hooks in `hooks/hooks.json`:\n   343→\n   344→```json\n   345→{\n   346→  \"PreToolUse\": [\n   347→    {\n   348→      \"matcher\": \"Write|Edit\",\n   349→      \"hooks\": [\n   350→        {\n   351→          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n   352→          \"prompt\": \"Validate file write safety\"\n   353→        }\n   354→      ]\n   355→    }\n   356→  ],\n   357→  \"Stop\": [\n   358→    {\n   359→      \"matcher\": \"*\",\n   360→      \"hooks\": [\n   361→        {\n   362→          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n   363→          \"prompt\": \"Verify task completion\"\n   364→        }\n   365→      ]\n   366→    }\n   367→  ],\n   368→  \"SessionStart\": [\n   369→    {\n   370→      \"matcher\": \"*\",\n   371→      \"hooks\": [\n   372→        {\n   373→          \"type\": \"command\",\n   374→          \"command\": \"bash ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/scripts/load-context.sh\",\n   375→          \"timeout\": 10\n   376→        }\n   377→      ]\n   378→    }\n   379→  ]\n   380→}\n   381→```\n   382→\n   383→Plugin hooks merge with user's hooks and run in parallel.\n   384→\n   385→## Matchers\n   386→\n   387→### Tool Name Matching\n   388→\n   389→**Exact match:**\n   390→```json\n   391→\"matcher\": \"Write\"\n   392→```\n   393→\n   394→**Multiple tools:**\n   395→```json\n   396→\"matcher\": \"Read|Write|Edit\"\n   397→```\n   398→\n   399→**Wildcard (all tools):**\n   400→```json\n   401→\"matcher\": \"*\"\n   402→```\n   403→\n   404→**Regex patterns:**\n   405→```json\n   406→\"matcher\": \"mcp__.*__delete.*\"  // All MCP delete tools\n   407→```\n   408→\n   409→**Note:** Matchers are case-sensitive.\n   410→\n   411→### Common Patterns\n   412→\n   413→```json\n   414→// All MCP tools\n   415→\"matcher\": \"mcp__.*\"\n   416→\n   417→// Specific plugin's MCP tools\n   418→\"matcher\": \"mcp__plugin_asana_.*\"\n   419→\n   420→// All file operations\n   421→\"matcher\": \"Read|Write|Edit\"\n   422→\n   423→// Bash commands only\n   424→\"matcher\": \"Bash\"\n   425→```\n   426→\n   427→## Security Best Practices\n   428→\n   429→### Input Validation\n   430→\n   431→Always validate inputs in command hooks:\n   432→\n   433→```bash\n   434→#!/bin/bash\n   435→set -euo pipefail\n   436→\n   437→input=$(cat)\n   438→tool_name=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_name')\n   439→\n   440→# Validate tool name format\n   441→if [[ ! \"$tool_name\" =~ ^[a-zA-Z0-9_]+$ ]]; then\n   442→  echo '{\"decision\": \"deny\", \"reason\": \"Invalid tool name\"}' >&2\n   443→  exit 2\n   444→fi\n   445→```\n   446→\n   447→### Path Safety\n   448→\n   449→Check for path traversal and sensitive files:\n   450→\n   451→```bash\n   452→file_path=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_input.file_path')\n   453→\n   454→# Deny path traversal\n   455→if [[ \"$file_path\" == *\"..\"* ]]; then\n   456→  echo '{\"decision\": \"deny\", \"reason\": \"Path traversal detected\"}' >&2\n   457→  exit 2\n   458→fi\n   459→\n   460→# Deny sensitive files\n   461→if [[ \"$file_path\" == *\".env\"* ]]; then\n   462→  echo '{\"decision\": \"deny\", \"reason\": \"Sensitive file\"}' >&2\n   463→  exit 2\n   464→fi\n   465→```\n   466→\n   467→See `examples/validate-write.sh` and `examples/validate-bash.sh` for complete examples.\n   468→\n   469→### Quote All Variables\n   470→\n   471→```bash\n   472→# GOOD: Quoted\n   473→echo \"$file_path\"\n   474→cd \"$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR\"\n   475→\n   476→# BAD: Unquoted (injection risk)\n   477→echo $file_path\n   478→cd $CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR\n   479→```\n   480→\n   481→### Set Appropriate Timeouts\n   482→\n   483→```json\n   484→{\n   485→  \"type\": \"command\",\n   486→  \"command\": \"bash script.sh\",\n   487→  \"timeout\": 10\n   488→}\n   489→```\n   490→\n   491→**Defaults:** Command hooks (60s), Prompt hooks (30s)\n   492→\n   493→## Performance Considerations\n   494→\n   495→### Parallel Execution\n   496→\n   497→All matching hooks run **in parallel**:\n   498→\n   499→```json\n   500→{\n   501→  \"PreToolUse\": [\n   502→    {\n   503→      \"matcher\": \"Write\",\n   504→      \"hooks\": [\n   505→        {\"type\": \"command\", \"command\": \"check1.sh\"},  // Parallel\n   506→        {\"type\": \"command\", \"command\": \"check2.sh\"},  // Parallel\n   507→        {\"type\": \"prompt\", \"prompt\": \"Validate...\"}   // Parallel\n   508→      ]\n   509→    }\n   510→  ]\n   511→}\n   512→```\n   513→\n   514→**Design implications:**\n   515→- Hooks don't see each other's output\n   516→- Non-deterministic ordering\n   517→- Design for independence\n   518→\n   519→### Optimization\n   520→\n   521→1. Use command hooks for quick deterministic checks\n   522→2. Use prompt hooks for complex reasoning\n   523→3. Cache validation results in temp files\n   524→4. Minimize I/O in hot paths\n   525→\n   526→## Temporarily Active Hooks\n   527→\n   528→Create hooks that activate conditionally by checking for a flag file or configuration:\n   529→\n   530→**Pattern: Flag file activation**\n   531→```bash\n   532→#!/bin/bash\n   533→# Only active when flag file exists\n   534→FLAG_FILE=\"$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/.enable-strict-validation\"\n   535→\n   536→if [ ! -f \"$FLAG_FILE\" ]; then\n   537→  # Flag not present, skip validation\n   538→  exit 0\n   539→fi\n   540→\n   541→# Flag present, run validation\n   542→input=$(cat)\n   543→# ... validation logic ...\n   544→```\n   545→\n   546→**Pattern: Configuration-based activation**\n   547→```bash\n   548→#!/bin/bash\n   549→# Check configuration for activation\n   550→CONFIG_FILE=\"$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/.claude/plugin-config.json\"\n   551→\n   552→if [ -f \"$CONFIG_FILE\" ]; then\n   553→  enabled=$(jq -r '.strictMode // false' \"$CONFIG_FILE\")\n   554→  if [ \"$enabled\" != \"true\" ]; then\n   555→    exit 0  # Not enabled, skip\n   556→  fi\n   557→fi\n   558→\n   559→# Enabled, run hook logic\n   560→input=$(cat)\n   561→# ... hook logic ...\n   562→```\n   563→\n   564→**Use cases:**\n   565→- Enable strict validation only when needed\n   566→- Temporary debugging hooks\n   567→- Project-specific hook behavior\n   568→- Feature flags for hooks\n   569→\n   570→**Best practice:** Document activation mechanism in plugin README so users know how to enable/disable temporary hooks.\n   571→\n   572→## Hook Lifecycle and Limitations\n   573→\n   574→### Hooks Load at Session Start\n   575→\n   576→**Important:** Hooks are loaded when Claude Code session starts. Changes to hook configuration require restarting Claude Code.\n   577→\n   578→**Cannot hot-swap hooks:**\n   579→- Editing `hooks/hooks.json` won't affect current session\n   580→- Adding new hook scripts won't be recognized\n   581→- Changing hook commands/prompts won't update\n   582→- Must restart Claude Code: exit and run `claude` again\n   583→\n   584→**To test hook changes:**\n   585→1. Edit hook configuration or scripts\n   586→2. Exit Claude Code session\n   587→3. Restart: `claude` or `cc`\n   588→4. New hook configuration loads\n   589→5. Test hooks with `claude --debug`\n   590→\n   591→### Hook Validation at Startup\n   592→\n   593→Hooks are validated when Claude Code starts:\n   594→- Invalid JSON in hooks.json causes loading failure\n   595→- Missing scripts cause warnings\n   596→- Syntax errors reported in debug mode\n   597→\n   598→Use `/hooks` command to review loaded hooks in current session.\n   599→\n   600→## Debugging Hooks\n   601→\n   602→### Enable Debug Mode\n   603→\n   604→```bash\n   605→claude --debug\n   606→```\n   607→\n   608→Look for hook registration, execution logs, input/output JSON, and 623→Ensure hooks output valid JSON:\n   624→\n   625→```bash\n   626→output=$(./your-hook.sh < test-input.json)\n   627→echo \"$output\" | jq .\n   628→```\n   629→\n   630→## Quick Reference\n   631→\n   632→### Hook Events Summary\n   633→\n   634→| Event | When | Use For |\n   635→|-------|------|---------|\n   636→| PreToolUse | Before tool | Validation, modification |\n   637→| is non-greedy (takes FIRST tag), whitespace normalized\n   133→  PROMISE_TEXT=$(echo \"$LAST_OUTPUT\" | perl -0777 -pe 's/.*?<promise>(.*?)<\\/promise>.*/$1/s; s/^\\s+|\\s+$//g; s/\\s+/ /g' 2>/dev/null || echo \"\")\n   134→\n   135→  # Use = for literal string comparison (not pattern matching)\n   136→  # == in [[ ]] does glob pattern matching which breaks with *, ?, [ characters\n   137→  if [[ -n \"$PROMISE_TEXT\" ]] && [[ \"$PROMISE_TEXT\" = \"$COMPLETION_PROMISE\" ]]; then\n   138→    echo \"✅ Ralph loop: Detected <promise>$COMPLETION_PROMISE</promise>\"\n   139→    rm \"$RALPH_STATE_FILE\"\n   140→    exit 0\n   141→  fi\n   142→fi\n   143→\n   144→# Not complete - continue loop with SAME PROMPT\n   145→NEXT_ITERATION=$((ITERATION + 1))\n   146→\n   147→# Extract prompt (everything after the closing ---)\n   148→# Skip first --- line, skip until second --- line, then print everything after\n   149→# Use i>=2 instead of i==2 to handle --- in prompt content\n   150→PROMPT_TEXT=$(awk '/^---$/{i++; next} i>=2' \"$RALPH_STATE_FILE\")\n   151→\n   152→if [[ -z \"$PROMPT_TEXT\" ]]; then\n   153→  echo \"⚠️  Ralph loop: State file corrupted or incomplete\" >&2\n   154→  echo \"   File: $RALPH_STATE_FILE\" >&2\n   155→  echo \"   Problem: No prompt text found\" >&2\n   156→  echo \"\" >&2\n   157→  echo \"   This usually means:\" >&2\n   158→  echo \"     • State file was manually edited\" >&2\n   159→  echo \"     • File was corrupted during writing\" >&2\n   160→  echo \"\" >&2\n   161→  echo \"   Ralph loop is stopping. {"parentUuid":"87f06d63-2d63-4e89-8abe-3fa67199f877","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"4cff8217-4055-4c23-8140-7e344f8eaa3c","agentId":"afe9d1f61c02b1e8d","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01F4CnhcFApAFWHPT5dpmiDH","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Advanced Hook Use Cases\n     2→\n     3→This reference covers advanced hook patterns and techniques for sophisticated automation workflows.\n     4→\n     5→## Multi-Stage Validation\n     6→\n     7→Combine command and prompt hooks for layered validation:\n     8→\n     9→```json\n    10→{\n    11→  \"PreToolUse\": [\n    12→    {\n    13→      \"matcher\": \"Bash\",\n    14→      \"hooks\": [\n    15→        {\n    16→          \"type\": \"command\",\n    17→          \"command\": \"bash ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/scripts/quick-check.sh\",\n    18→          \"timeout\": 5\n    19→        },\n    20→        {\n    21→          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n    22→          \"prompt\": \"Deep analysis of bash command: $TOOL_INPUT\",\n    23→          \"timeout\": 15\n    24→        }\n    25→      ]\n    26→    }\n    27→  ]\n    28→}\n    29→```\n    30→\n    31→**Use case:** Fast deterministic checks followed by intelligent analysis\n    32→\n    33→**Example quick-check.sh:**\n    34→```bash\n    35→#!/bin/bash\n    36→input=$(cat)\n    37→command=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_input.command')\n    38→\n    39→# Immediate approval for safe commands\n    40→if [[ \"$command\" =~ ^(ls|pwd|echo|date|whoami)$ ]]; then\n    41→  exit 0\n    42→fi\n    43→\n    44→# Let prompt hook handle complex cases\n    45→exit 0\n    46→```\n    47→\n    48→The command hook quickly approves obviously safe commands, while the prompt hook analyzes everything else.\n    49→\n    50→## Conditional Hook Execution\n    51→\n    52→Execute hooks based on environment or context:\n    53→\n    54→```bash\n    55→#!/bin/bash\n    56→# Only run in CI environment\n    57→if [ -z \"$CI\" ]; then\n    58→  echo '{\"continue\": true}' # Skip in non-CI\n    59→  exit 0\n    60→fi\n    61→\n    62→# Run validation logic in CI\n    63→input=$(cat)\n    64→# ... validation code ...\n    65→```\n    66→\n    67→**Use cases:**\n    68→- Different behavior in CI vs local development\n    69→- Project-specific validation\n    70→- User-specific rules\n    71→\n    72→**Example: Skip certain checks for trusted users:**\n    73→```bash\n    74→#!/bin/bash\n    75→# Skip detailed checks for admin users\n    76→if [ \"$USER\" = \"admin\" ]; then\n    77→  exit 0\n    78→fi\n    79→\n    80→# Full validation for other users\n    81→input=$(cat)\n    82→# ... validation code ...\n    83→```\n    84→\n    85→## Hook Chaining via State\n    86→\n    87→Share state between hooks using temporary files:\n    88→\n    89→```bash\n    90→# Hook 1: Analyze and save state\n    91→#!/bin/bash\n    92→input=$(cat)\n    93→command=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_input.command')\n    94→\n    95→# Analyze command\n    96→risk_level=$(calculate_risk \"$command\")\n    97→echo \"$risk_level\" > /tmp/hook-state-$$\n    98→\n    99→exit 0\n   100→```\n   101→\n   102→```bash\n   103→# Hook 2: Use saved state\n   104→#!/bin/bash\n   105→risk_level=$(cat /tmp/hook-state-$$ 2>/dev/null || echo \"unknown\")\n   106→\n   107→if [ \"$risk_level\" = \"high\" ]; then\n   108→  echo \"High risk operation detected\" >&2\n   109→  exit 2\n   110→fi\n   111→```\n   112→\n   113→**Important:** This only works for sequential hook events (e.g., PreToolUse then PostToolUse), not parallel hooks.\n   114→\n   115→## Dynamic Hook Configuration\n   116→\n   117→Modify hook behavior based on project configuration:\n   118→\n   119→```bash\n   120→#!/bin/bash\n   121→cd \"$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR\" || exit 1\n   122→\n   123→# Read project-specific config\n   124→if [ -f \".claude-hooks-config.json\" ]; then\n   125→  strict_mode=$(jq -r '.strict_mode' .claude-hooks-config.json)\n   126→\n   127→  if [ \"$strict_mode\" = \"true\" ]; then\n   128→    # Apply strict validation\n   129→    # ...\n   130→  else\n   131→    # Apply lenient validation\n   132→    # ...\n   133→  fi\n   134→fi\n   135→```\n   136→\n   137→**Example .claude-hooks-config.json:**\n   138→```json\n   139→{\n   140→  \"strict_mode\": true,\n   141→  \"allowed_commands\": [\"ls\", \"pwd\", \"grep\"],\n   142→  \"forbidden_paths\": [\"/etc\", \"/sys\"]\n   143→}\n   144→```\n   145→\n   146→## Context-Aware Prompt Hooks\n   147→\n   148→Use transcript and session context for intelligent decisions:\n   149→\n   150→```json\n   151→{\n   152→  \"Stop\": [\n   153→    {\n   154→      \"matcher\": \"*\",\n   155→      \"hooks\": [\n   156→        {\n   157→          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n   158→          \"prompt\": \"Review the full transcript at $TRANSCRIPT_PATH. Check: 1) Were tests run after code changes? 2) Did the build succeed? 3) Were all user questions answered? 4) Is there any unfinished work? Return 'approve' only if everything is complete.\"\n   159→        }\n   160→      ]\n   161→    }\n   162→  ]\n   163→}\n   164→```\n   165→\n   166→The LLM can read the transcript file and make context-aware decisions.\n   167→\n   168→## Performance Optimization\n   169→\n   170→### Caching Validation Results\n   171→\n   172→```bash\n   173→#!/bin/bash\n   174→input=$(cat)\n   175→file_path=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_input.file_path')\n   176→cache_key=$(echo -n \"$file_path\" | md5sum | cut -d' ' -f1)\n   177→cache_file=\"/tmp/hook-cache-$cache_key\"\n   178→\n   179→# Check cache\n   180→if [ -f \"$cache_file\" ]; then\n   181→  cache_age=$(($(date +%s) - $(stat -f%m \"$cache_file\" 2>/dev/null || stat -c%Y \"$cache_file\")))\n   182→  if [ \"$cache_age\" -lt 300 ]; then  # 5 minute cache\n   183→    cat \"$cache_file\"\n   184→    exit 0\n   185→  fi\n   186→fi\n   187→\n   188→# Perform validation\n   189→result='{\"decision\": \"approve\"}'\n   190→\n   191→# Cache result\n   192→echo \"$result\" > \"$cache_file\"\n   193→echo \"$result\"\n   194→```\n   195→\n   196→### Parallel Execution Optimization\n   197→\n   198→Since hooks run in parallel, design them to be independent:\n   199→\n   200→```json\n   201→{\n   202→  \"PreToolUse\": [\n   203→    {\n   204→      \"matcher\": \"Write\",\n   205→      \"hooks\": [\n   206→        {\n   207→          \"type\": \"command\",\n   208→          \"command\": \"bash check-size.sh\",      // Independent\n   209→          \"timeout\": 2\n   210→        },\n   211→        {\n   212→          \"type\": \"command\",\n   213→          \"command\": \"bash check-path.sh\",      // Independent\n   214→          \"timeout\": 2\n   215→        },\n   216→        {\n   217→          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n   218→          \"prompt\": \"Check content safety\",     // Independent\n   219→          \"timeout\": 10\n   220→        }\n   221→      ]\n   222→    }\n   223→  ]\n   224→}\n   225→```\n   226→\n   227→All three hooks run simultaneously, reducing total latency.\n   228→\n   229→## Cross-Event Workflows\n   230→\n   231→Coordinate hooks across different events:\n   232→\n   233→**SessionStart - Set up tracking:**\n   234→```bash\n   235→#!/bin/bash\n   236→# Initialize session tracking\n   237→echo \"0\" > /tmp/test-count-$$\n   238→echo \"0\" > /tmp/build-count-$$\n   239→```\n   240→\n   241→**PostToolUse - Track events:**\n   242→```bash\n   243→#!/bin/bash\n   244→input=$(cat)\n   245→tool_name=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_name')\n   246→\n   247→if [ \"$tool_name\" = \"Bash\" ]; then\n   248→  command=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_result')\n   249→  if [[ \"$command\" == *\"test\"* ]]; then\n   250→    count=$(cat /tmp/test-count-$$ 2>/dev/null || echo \"0\")\n   251→    echo $((count + 1)) > /tmp/test-count-$$\n   252→  fi\n   253→fi\n   254→```\n   255→\n   256→**Stop - Verify based on tracking:**\n   257→```bash\n   258→#!/bin/bash\n   259→test_count=$(cat /tmp/test-count-$$ 2>/dev/null || echo \"0\")\n   260→\n   261→if [ \"$test_count\" -eq 0 ]; then\n   262→  echo '{\"decision\": \"block\", \"reason\": \"No tests were run\"}' >&2\n   263→  exit 2\n   264→fi\n   265→```\n   266→\n   267→## Integration with External Systems\n   268→\n   269→### Slack Notifications\n   270→\n   271→```bash\n   272→#!/bin/bash\n   273→input=$(cat)\n   274→tool_name=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_name')\n   275→decision=\"blocked\"\n   276→\n   277→# Send notification to Slack\n   278→curl -X POST \"$SLACK_WEBHOOK\" \\\n   279→  -H 'Content-Type: application/json' \\\n   280→  -d \"{\\\"text\\\": \\\"Hook ${decision} ${tool_name} operation\\\"}\" \\\n   281→  2>/dev/null\n   282→\n   283→echo '{\"decision\": \"deny\"}' >&2\n   284→exit 2\n   285→```\n   286→\n   287→### Database Logging\n   288→\n   289→```bash\n   290→#!/bin/bash\n   291→input=$(cat)\n   292→\n   293→# Log to database\n   294→psql \"$DATABASE_URL\" -c \"INSERT INTO hook_logs (event, data) VALUES ('PreToolUse', '$input')\" \\\n   295→  2>/dev/null\n   296→\n   297→exit 0\n   298→```\n   299→\n   300→### Metrics Collection\n   301→\n   302→```bash\n   303→#!/bin/bash\n   304→input=$(cat)\n   305→tool_name=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_name')\n   306→\n   307→# Send metrics to monitoring system\n   308→echo \"hook.pretooluse.${tool_name}:1|c\" | nc -u -w1 statsd.local 8125\n   309→\n   310→exit 0\n   311→```\n   312→\n   313→## Security Patterns\n   314→\n   315→### Rate Limiting\n   316→\n   317→```bash\n   318→#!/bin/bash\n   319→input=$(cat)\n   320→command=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_input.command')\n   321→\n   322→# Track command frequency\n   323→rate_file=\"/tmp/hook-rate-$$\"\n   324→current_minute=$(date +%Y%m%d%H%M)\n   325→\n   326→if [ -f \"$rate_file\" ]; then\n   327→  last_minute=$(head -1 \"$rate_file\")\n   328→  count=$(tail -1 \"$rate_file\")\n   329→\n   330→  if [ \"$current_minute\" = \"$last_minute\" ]; then\n   331→    if [ \"$count\" -gt 10 ]; then\n   332→      echo '{\"decision\": \"deny\", \"reason\": \"Rate limit exceeded\"}' >&2\n   333→      exit 2\n   334→    fi\n   335→    count=$((count + 1))\n   336→  else\n   337→    count=1\n   338→  fi\n   339→else\n   340→  count=1\n   341→fi\n   342→\n   343→echo \"$current_minute\" > \"$rate_file\"\n   344→echo \"$count\" >> \"$rate_file\"\n   345→\n   346→exit 0\n   347→```\n   348→\n   349→### Audit Logging\n   350→\n   351→```bash\n   352→#!/bin/bash\n   353→input=$(cat)\n   354→tool_name=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_name')\n   355→timestamp=$(date -Iseconds)\n   356→\n   357→# Append to audit log\n   358→echo \"$timestamp | $USER | $tool_name | $input\" >> ~/.claude/audit.log\n   359→\n   360→exit 0\n   361→```\n   362→\n   363→### Secret Detection\n   364→\n   365→```bash\n   366→#!/bin/bash\n   367→input=$(cat)\n   368→content=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_input.content')\n   369→\n   370→# Check for common secret patterns\n   371→if echo \"$content\" | grep -qE \"(api[_-]?key|password|secret|token).{0,20}['\\\"]?[A-Za-z0-9]{20,}\"; then\n   372→  echo '{\"decision\": \"deny\", \"reason\": \"Potential secret detected in content\"}' >&2\n   373→  exit 2\n   374→fi\n   375→\n   376→exit 0\n   377→```\n   378→\n   379→## Testing Advanced Hooks\n   380→\n   381→### Unit Testing Hook Scripts\n   382→\n   383→```bash\n   384→# test-hook.sh\n   385→#!/bin/bash\n   386→\n   387→# Test 1: Approve safe command\n   388→result=$(echo '{\"tool_input\": {\"command\": \"ls\"}}' | bash validate-bash.sh)\n   389→if [ $? -eq 0 ]; then\n   420→  echo \"✓ SessionStart hook works\"\n   421→else\n   422→  echo \"✗ SessionStart hook failed\"\n   423→fi\n   424→\n   425→# Clean up\n   426→rm -rf \"$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR\"\n   427→```\n   428→\n   429→## Best Practices for Advanced Hooks\n   430→\n   431→1. **Keep hooks independent**: Don't rely on execution order\n   432→2. **Use timeouts**: Set appropriate limits for each hook type\n   433→3. **Handle errors gracefully**: Provide clear error messages\n   434→4. **Document complexity**: Explain advanced patterns in README\n   435→5. **Test thoroughly**: Cover edge cases and failure modes\n   436→6. **Monitor performance**: Track hook execution time\n   437→7. **Version configuration**: Use version control for hook configs\n   438→8. **Provide escape hatches**: Allow users to bypass hooks when needed\n   439→\n   440→## Common Pitfalls\n   441→\n   442→### ❌ Assuming Hook Order\n   443→\n   444→```bash\n   445→# BAD: Assumes hooks run in specific order\n   446→# Hook 1 saves state, Hook 2 reads it\n   447→# This can fail because hooks run in parallel!\n   448→```\n   449→\n   450→### ❌ Long-Running Hooks\n   451→\n   452→```bash\n   453→# BAD: Hook takes 2 minutes to run\n   454→sleep 120\n   455→# This will timeout and block the workflow\n   456→```\n   457→\n   458→### ❌ Uncaught Exceptions\n   459→\n   460→```bash\n   461→# BAD: Script crashes on unexpected input\n   462→file_path=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_input.file_path')\n   463→cat \"$file_path\"  # Fails if file doesn't exist\n   464→```\n   465→\n   466→### ✅ Proper Error Handling\n   467→\n   468→```bash\n   469→# GOOD: Handles errors gracefully\n   470→file_path=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_input.file_path')\n   471→if [ ! -f \"$file_path\" ]; then\n   472→  echo '{\"continue\": true, \"systemMessage\": \"File not found, skipping check\"}' >&2\n   473→  exit 0\n   474→fi\n   475→```\n   476→\n   477→## Conclusion\n   478→\n   479→Advanced hook patterns enable sophisticated automation while maintaining reliability and performance. {"parentUuid":"a99b0132-c25d-4678-8a1c-f0a1a6195628","isSidechain":true,"agentId":"afe9d1f61c02b1e8d","message":{"model":"claude-opus-4-6","id":"msg_011zDEouRcDv35BbWQq7dG5u","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"\n\nI now have all the data needed for a comprehensive report. Let me compile everything.\n\n---\n\n# Claude Code Hooks -- Mechanical Enforcement of Pipeline Discipline\n\n## Research Report\n\n---\n\n## 1. COMPLETE HOOK EVENT INVENTORY\n\nBased on the plugin-dev SKILL.md (the authoritative reference found at `/Users/mohamedabdallah/.claude/plugins/marketplaces/claude-plugins-official/plugins/plugin-dev/skills/hook-development/SKILL.md`) and confirmed by real implementations, Claude Code supports **9 hook events**:\n\n| Event | When It Fires | Can Block? | Can Modify? | Sync? |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| **PreToolUse** | Before any tool executes | YES (deny) | YES (updatedInput) | Sync -- tool waits |\n| **PostToolUse** | After tool completes | NO (tool already ran) | NO | Sync -- result waits |\n| **Stop** | Agent decides to stop | YES (block) | YES (inject reason as next prompt) | Sync -- stop waits |\n| **SubagentStop** | Subagent decides to stop | YES (block) | YES (same as Stop) | Sync |\n| **UserPromptSubmit** | User submits a prompt | Unclear (can add context) | YES (can add context) | Sync |\n| **SessionStart** | Session begins | NO | YES (inject context, set env vars) | Sync |\n| **SessionEnd** | Session ends | NO | NO | Fire-and-forget |\n| **PreCompact** | Before context compaction | NO | YES (inject text to preserve) | Sync |\n| **Notification** | Claude sends notification | NO | NO | Fire-and-forget |\n\n### Stdin Payloads (per event)\n\nAll hooks receive JSON on stdin with these **common fields**:\n```json\n{\n  \"session_id\": \"abc123\",\n  \"transcript_path\": \"/path/to/transcript.txt\",\n  \"cwd\": \"/current/working/dir\",\n  \"permission_mode\": \"ask|allow\",\n  \"hook_event_name\": \"PreToolUse|PostToolUse|Stop|...\"\n}\n```\n\n**Event-specific additional fields:**\n- **PreToolUse / PostToolUse**: `tool_name`, `tool_input`, `tool_result` (PostToolUse only)\n- **Stop / SubagentStop**: `reason`\n- **UserPromptSubmit**: `user_prompt`\n- **SessionStart**: matcher supports `startup|resume|clear|compact`\n\n### Environment Variables Available to All Hooks:\n- `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` -- project root\n- `$CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT` -- plugin directory (for portable paths)\n- `$CLAUDE_ENV_FILE` -- SessionStart only: write env vars here to persist them\n- `$CLAUDE_CODE_REMOTE` -- set if running in remote context\n\n---\n\n## 2. THE STOP HOOK -- \"Can it prevent the agent from completing?\"\n\n**YES.** This is the single most important finding.\n\n### Mechanism\n\nThe Stop hook can return:\n```json\n{\n  \"decision\": \"block\",\n  \"reason\": \"You haven't run tests yet. Run tests before stopping.\",\n  \"systemMessage\": \"Additional context for Claude\"\n}\n```\n\nWhen `decision` is `\"block\"`:\n1. The agent does NOT stop.\n2. The `reason` field is fed back to Claude as the **next user prompt** -- the agent continues working with that reason as its instructions.\n3. The `systemMessage` is injected into Claude's context.\n\nWhen `decision` is `\"approve\"` (or hook exits 0 with no block):\n- The agent stops normally.\n\n### Live Proof: ralph-loop\n\nThe ralph-loop plugin (`/Users/mohamedabdallah/.claude/plugins/marketplaces/claude-plugins-official/plugins/ralph-loop/hooks/stop-hook.sh`) is a 192-line production implementation that:\n\n1. Reads a state file (`.claude/ralph-loop.local.md`) to check if a loop is active\n2. Checks iteration count against max_iterations\n3. Reads the transcript to find the last assistant message\n4. Checks for a `<promise>completion text</promise>` tag\n5. If the loop is not complete, returns `{\"decision\": \"block\", \"reason\": \"<the prompt to re-execute>\"}` -- which feeds the prompt back to Claude, creating an autonomous loop\n6. Session isolation via `session_id` matching\n\n**This is the definitive proof that Stop hooks can prevent completion and force the agent to continue.**\n\n### hookify's Stop hook\n\nThe hookify plugin (`require-tests-stop.local.md`) shows a simpler pattern:\n```yaml\nname: require-tests-run\nevent: stop\naction: block\nconditions:\n  - field: transcript\n    operator: not_contains\n    pattern: npm test|pytest|cargo test\n```\n\nThis reads the transcript file and blocks stopping if no test commands appear. The rule engine returns:\n```json\n{\n  \"decision\": \"block\",\n  \"reason\": \"Tests not detected in transcript!\",\n  \"systemMessage\": \"Before stopping, please run tests...\"\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. PreToolUse BLOCKING -- \"Can we block git commit if no proof exists?\"\n\n**YES.** PreToolUse is the most powerful enforcement point.\n\n### Three Response Modes\n\nA PreToolUse hook can return `hookSpecificOutput` with:\n\n**a) DENY -- Block the tool call entirely:**\n```json\n{\n  \"hookSpecificOutput\": {\n    \"hookEventName\": \"PreToolUse\",\n    \"permissionDecision\": \"deny\"\n  },\n  \"systemMessage\": \"Cannot commit: no proof artifacts found.\"\n}\n```\n\n**b) ASK -- Escalate to user for approval:**\n```json\n{\n  \"hookSpecificOutput\": {\n    \"hookEventName\": \"PreToolUse\",\n    \"permissionDecision\": \"ask\"\n  },\n  \"systemMessage\": \"Writing to sensitive file, needs user approval.\"\n}\n```\n\n**c) MODIFY -- Rewrite the tool input silently:**\n```json\n{\n  \"hookSpecificOutput\": {\n    \"hookEventName\": \"PreToolUse\",\n    \"updatedInput\": {\n      \"command\": \"echo 'Blocked: you must use context-mode tools instead.'\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Exit Code Semantics\n- **Exit 0**: Allow (stdout shown in transcript)\n- **Exit 2**: Block (stderr fed back to Claude as error)\n- **Non-zero (other)**: Non-blocking error\n\n### Live Proof: context-mode pretooluse.mjs\n\nThe hook at `/Users/mohamedabdallah/.claude/plugins/marketplaces/claude-context-mode/hooks/pretooluse.mjs` is actively blocking tool calls in this very session:\n\n- **WebFetch** calls: returns `permissionDecision: \"deny\"` with a redirect message\n- **Bash curl/wget**: rewrites the command via `updatedInput` to an echo statement\n- **Task (subagent)**: injects routing instructions into the prompt via `updatedInput`\n\nThis hook blocked my attempt to fetch the official docs, which is itself proof that the enforcement is mechanical and cannot be rationalized away.\n\n### Live Proof: protected-path-write-guard\n\nThe Wazir hook at `/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir/hooks/protected-path-write-guard` blocks Write/Edit to protected paths:\n- Reads the manifest's `protected_paths` list\n- Checks if target file is under a protected directory\n- Returns exit 42 (non-zero = block) if blocked, exit 0 if allowed\n- The agent never gets to write -- the tool call is denied before execution\n\n### Blocking git commit\n\nTo block `git commit` if no proof exists, you would register:\n```json\n{\n  \"PreToolUse\": [\n    {\n      \"matcher\": \"Bash\",\n      \"hooks\": [\n        {\n          \"type\": \"command\",\n          \"command\": \"./hooks/proof-gate-guard\"\n        }\n      ]\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\nThe guard script would:\n1. Parse stdin JSON, extract `tool_input.command`\n2. Check if command starts with `git commit`\n3. If so, check for proof artifact files on disk\n4. If no proof found: exit 2 with deny JSON\n5. If proof found: exit 0\n\n---\n\n## 4. STATE TRACKING ACROSS A SESSION\n\nHooks are stateless processes -- each invocation is a fresh process. But there are multiple proven patterns for cross-invocation state:\n\n### Pattern A: File-Based State (Most Common)\n\n**Proven in ralph-loop** (`.claude/ralph-loop.local.md`):\n- YAML frontmatter tracks iteration count, session_id, completion_promise\n- Each Stop hook invocation reads the file, updates iteration, writes it back\n- Atomic update via temp file + mv\n\n**Proven in Wazir's loop-cap-guard** (`~/.wazir/projects/<slug>/runs/<run-id>/status.json`):\n- Reads `phase_loop_counts` from a JSON status file\n- Compares against configured cap\n- The status file is updated by the CLI between iterations\n\n**Proven in context-mode router** (routing.ndjson log):\n- Appends decisions to an NDJSON log file\n- Could be read by later hooks to check history\n\n### Pattern B: Flag Files\n\nFrom the advanced.md reference:\n```bash\nFLAG_FILE=\"$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/.enable-strict-validation\"\nif [ ! -f \"$FLAG_FILE\" ]; then\n  exit 0  # Skip\nfi\n```\n\nFor pipeline enforcement: a SessionStart hook creates `~/.wazir/projects/<slug>/runs/<run-id>/phase-gate.json`, and each PreToolUse/Stop hook reads it.\n\n### Pattern C: SessionStart Environment Variables\n\nSessionStart hooks can persist env vars via `$CLAUDE_ENV_FILE`:\n```bash\necho \"export PIPELINE_PHASE=clarifier\" >> \"$CLAUDE_ENV_FILE\"\necho \"export RESEARCH_DONE=false\" >> \"$CLAUDE_ENV_FILE\"\n```\n\nThese would be available to all subsequent hooks in the session. **However**, this only sets the initial state -- subsequent hooks cannot update these env vars for other hooks (each hook is a separate process).\n\n### Pattern D: Cross-Event Tracking via Temp Files\n\nFrom the advanced.md reference, using PID-namespaced temp files:\n```bash\n# SessionStart: echo \"0\" > /tmp/test-count-$$\n# PostToolUse: increment count on test detection\n# Stop: check count > 0\n```\n\n**Limitation**: `$$` is the hook process PID, not the Claude session PID. For reliable cross-hook state, use `$SESSION_ID` from the stdin payload or a fixed project-scoped path.\n\n### Recommended Architecture for Pipeline State Machine\n\nUse a **single JSON state file** per run:\n```\n~/.wazir/projects/<slug>/runs/<run-id>/pipeline-state.json\n```\n\nContents:\n```json\n{\n  \"phase\": \"executor\",\n  \"gates_passed\": {\n    \"research\": true,\n    \"clarification\": true,\n    \"planning\": true,\n    \"review\": false\n  },\n  \"proof_artifacts\": [\n    \"clarifier-proof.json\",\n    \"plan-proof.json\"\n  ],\n  \"updated_at\": \"2026-03-20T12:00:00Z\"\n}\n```\n\nEvery hook reads this file. The CLI updates it. No hook relies on env vars or PIDs.\n\n---\n\n## 5. HOOK TYPES -- COMMAND vs PROMPT\n\n### Command Hooks\n```json\n{\"type\": \"command\", \"command\": \"bash script.sh\", \"timeout\": 60}\n```\n- Execute arbitrary scripts (bash, node, python)\n- Deterministic, fast, predictable\n- Full control over exit codes and JSON output\n- **Best for enforcement** -- no ambiguity, no rationalization\n\n### Prompt Hooks (LLM-driven)\n```json\n{\"type\": \"prompt\", \"prompt\": \"Evaluate if this is appropriate: $TOOL_INPUT\", \"timeout\": 30}\n```\n- Supported on: **Stop, SubagentStop, UserPromptSubmit, PreToolUse**\n- Uses another LLM call to evaluate the condition\n- Context-aware: can reason about intent\n- **NOT suitable for enforcement** -- the LLM can rationalize, hallucinate, or be inconsistent\n\n### Verdict for Enforcement\n\n**Command hooks are the only viable option for mechanical enforcement.** Prompt hooks defeat the purpose because they re-introduce the same LLM rationalization problem you're trying to solve. A prompt hook that says \"check if tests were run\" can be talked out of blocking by the same reasoning patterns that cause the agent to skip tests in the first place.\n\n---\n\n## 6. REAL IMPLEMENTATIONS FOUND\n\n### 6.1 context-mode pretooluse.mjs (Active in this session)\n- **File**: `/Users/mohamedabdallah/.claude/plugins/marketplaces/claude-context-mode/hooks/pretooluse.mjs`\n- **What it does**: Blocks WebFetch, rewrites curl/wget Bash commands, injects context-mode routing into subagent prompts\n- **Enforcement technique**: `permissionDecision: \"deny\"` for hard blocks, `updatedInput` for silent rewrites\n\n### 6.2 ralph-loop stop-hook.sh\n- **File**: `/Users/mohamedabdallah/.claude/plugins/marketplaces/claude-plugins-official/plugins/ralph-loop/hooks/stop-hook.sh`\n- **What it does**: Prevents agent from stopping until a loop completes. Feeds the same prompt back on each iteration.\n- **Enforcement technique**: `\"decision\": \"block\"` with `\"reason\"` as re-injected prompt\n- **State**: `.claude/ralph-loop.local.md` with YAML frontmatter\n\n### 6.3 hookify rule engine\n- **Files**: `/Users/mohamedabdallah/.claude/plugins/marketplaces/claude-plugins-official/plugins/hookify/`\n- **What it does**: User-configurable rules in markdown files. Supports PreToolUse, PostToolUse, Stop, UserPromptSubmit.\n- **Enforcement technique**: Pattern matching (regex, contains, not_contains) on tool inputs, transcript, file paths\n- **Notable**: The `require-tests-stop` example blocks stopping if no test commands appear in transcript\n\n### 6.4 Wazir's own hooks (Active in this session)\n- **Files**: `/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir/hooks/`\n- **protected-path-write-guard**: Blocks Write/Edit to canonical paths (exit 42 = block)\n- **context-mode-router**: Routes large Bash output through context-mode (exit 1 = redirect)\n- **loop-cap-guard**: Prevents infinite loops by checking iteration count\n- **session-start**: Bootstraps skills and CLI guidance\n- **phase-prerequisite-guard**: (In tooling, not yet wired as a hook) Validates required artifacts and phase_exit events before allowing phase transitions\n\n---\n\n## 7. LIMITATIONS -- What Hooks CANNOT Do\n\n### 7.1 No Conversation History Access\nHooks receive the **current tool call** on stdin, not the full conversation. The only way to access history is via `transcript_path` (a JSONL file of all messages), which requires parsing. This is available in Stop/SubagentStop hooks but must be explicitly read and parsed by the hook script.\n\n### 7.2 No Agent Context/Reasoning Access\nHooks cannot see Claude's internal reasoning, chain of thought, or system prompt. They see only the tool call parameters and transcript.\n\n### 7.3 Hooks Are Loaded at Session Start\nChanges to `hooks.json` or hook scripts require restarting Claude Code. You cannot add/remove hooks mid-session. (However, hook *behavior* can change mid-session if the hook reads external state files that change.)\n\n### 7.4 Hooks Run in Parallel (Within a Matcher)\nMultiple hooks in the same array run in parallel. They cannot see each other's output. They cannot depend on each other's execution order. If one hook denies and another approves, the deny wins.\n\n### 7.5 No Inter-Hook Communication\nHook A cannot send data to Hook B within the same event. Each hook is an isolated process. State must be shared via the filesystem.\n\n### 7.6 Timeout Risk\nCommand hooks default to 60s timeout, prompt hooks to 30s. A hook that hangs or is too slow will be killed. For enforcement hooks, this means they should fail-closed (deny on timeout) rather than fail-open.\n\n### 7.7 PostToolUse Cannot Block\nPostToolUse fires after the tool has already executed. It can provide feedback (via systemMessage) or log, but it cannot undo the action. For enforcement, PreToolUse is the only option.\n\n### 7.8 SessionStart Cannot Block\nSessionStart hooks inject context and set environment, but they cannot prevent the session from starting. They can, however, set state that subsequent PreToolUse/Stop hooks check.\n\n### 7.9 Race Conditions\nIf two parallel hooks both read and write the same state file, there is a race condition. Use atomic operations (write to temp file, then mv) as ralph-loop does.\n\n---\n\n## 8. ANSWER: CAN WE BUILD AN ENFORCEMENT STATE MACHINE USING HOOKS?\n\n**Yes, definitively.** Here is the architecture:\n\n### The State Machine\n\n```\nSessionStart\n  |\n  v\n[Initialize pipeline-state.json: phase=init, gates_passed={}]\n  |\n  v\nPreToolUse:Bash (on git commit)\n  |-- Read pipeline-state.json\n  |-- Check: all required gates passed for current phase?\n  |-- NO  --> exit 2, deny with \"Missing prerequisites: research, review\"\n  |-- YES --> exit 0, allow\n  |\n  v\nPreToolUse:Write|Edit (on protected paths)\n  |-- Read pipeline-state.json\n  |-- Check: is current phase allowed to write this path?\n  |-- NO  --> exit 2, deny\n  |-- YES --> exit 0\n  |\n  v\nStop (on agent completion attempt)\n  |-- Read pipeline-state.json\n  |-- Check: all phases completed? All proofs present?\n  |-- NO  --> {\"decision\":\"block\", \"reason\":\"Phase review not complete. Run verification.\"}\n  |-- YES --> {\"decision\":\"approve\"}\n```\n\n### What Updates the State File?\n\nThe **CLI** (wazir capture) updates `pipeline-state.json` -- not the hooks. Hooks only **read** state and **enforce** gates. This separation is critical:\n- The agent calls `wazir capture phase-exit --phase clarifier --status completed`\n- The CLI validates and writes the phase_exit event\n- The next PreToolUse hook reads the updated state\n- Hooks never write to the state file (no race conditions)\n\n### Enforcement Points Available\n\n| What to enforce | Hook event | Matcher | Gate check |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| No commit without proof | PreToolUse | Bash | Parse command for `git commit`, check proof files exist |\n| No commit without review | PreToolUse | Bash | Parse command for `git commit`, check review-proof.json |\n| No write to protected paths | PreToolUse | Write\\|Edit | Check target path against manifest |\n| No stopping without all phases done | Stop | * | Check pipeline-state.json for completeness |\n| No skipping to executor without plan | PreToolUse | Bash | Parse command for phase-transition CLI calls |\n| Force test run before completion | Stop | * | Check transcript for test commands |\n| Cap loop iterations | SessionStart / PreToolUse | * | Check iteration count in state file |\n\n### Why This Works Where CLAUDE.md Instructions Fail\n\n1. **CLAUDE.md is advisory** -- the agent reads it and can rationalize exceptions. \"I'll skip the review because the change is trivial.\"\n2. **Hooks are mechanical** -- the process exits non-zero and the tool call is denied. There is no reasoning step. The agent cannot negotiate with exit code 2.\n3. **Git pre-push hooks are external** -- git runs them, not Claude. Same principle applies to Claude Code hooks: Claude Code (the runtime) runs them, not Claude (the model).\n\n### Key Design Principles\n\n1. **Command hooks only** -- never prompt hooks for enforcement\n2. **Fail closed** -- if state file is missing or corrupt, deny (not allow)\n3. **Read-only hooks** -- hooks read state, CLI writes state\n4. **Atomic state updates** -- temp file + mv for any hook that must write\n5. **Session-scoped** -- use session_id to avoid cross-session interference\n6. **Idempotent** -- hooks can fire multiple times for the same logical action\n\n### Files Relevant to This Research\n\n- `/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir/.claude/settings.json` -- active hook registration\n- `/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir/hooks/` -- all Wazir hook scripts\n- `/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir/tooling/src/guards/phase-prerequisite-guard.js` -- existing phase gate logic (not yet wired as a hook)\n-
